Slawson Exploration Company, Inc
Mooka 8-29-20TF2H
440' FSL & 1,140' FWL
SW SW Sec. 29, T152N, R92W
Big Bend Field/ Three Forks
Mountrail County, North Dakota
BOTTOM HOLE LOCATION:
9,701.57' north & 118.78' east of surface location or approx.
414.63' FNL & 1,258.78' FWL, NW NW Section 20 T152N R92W

WELL EVALUATION
View of Cyclone 5 tripping out upon reaching total depth at the Mooka 8-20-29TFH in Mountrail County, North
Dakota on September 9, 2014 (All photos by Gerald Jett, Sunburst Consulting).
INTRODUCTION
The Slawson Exploration Company, Inc. Mooka 8-29-20TF2H [SW SW Section 29, T152N,
R92W] is located approximately one mile south of New Town in Mountrail County, North Dakota.
The location lies within the Big Bend Field of the Williston Basin, where Slawson Exploration
Company, Inc. is producing from the Three Forks and using hydraulic fracturing techniques to
create new fractures and enhance natural fractures to draw from the pool.
The Mooka 8-29-20TF2H was planned as a two section lateral extending 9,409' at a heading of
0.97° from the SW quarter of the SW quadrant of Section 29, T152N, R92W to the NE quarter of
the NW quadrant of Section 20, T152N, R92W.
OFFSET WELLS
The primary offset well used to develop a prognosis of formation tops was the Slawson Exploration
Company, Inc. Mooka 6-29-20TFH, which is 40' east of the subject well.
The Slawson
Exploration Company, Inc., Hunter 8-8-17TF2H (2.16 miles south) and the Walleye Federal 12-
12-11TF3H, (3.22 miles north northwest) were also used as offset wells. Each of these wells
played an intricate part in landing of the build section for lateral operations.
ENGINEERING
The surface hole was spud August 18, 2014 and drilled to a depth of 1,924' MD with one 13 ½"
Atlas PDC bit in a time of 12.5 hours. Surface casing was set to 1,920' MD and consisted of 46
joints of 9 5/8" 36# J-55. The vertical hole was drilled with one 8 ¾" Reed DS616M PDC bit and
one Security MM65D bit to a KOP depth of 9,798' MD.
At kick-off point, the curve build began at 9,798' MD. Weatherford Directional Drilling Company
provided directional drilling and MWD personnel, tools and equipment. MWD surveys from the
vertical hole provided survey tie-in data for curve and lateral surveys. An Ulterra U516M PDC bit
ahead of a fixed 2.58° fixed motor drilled 853' of curve in 31.5 hours with a landing 83' below the
top of the Three Forks in the second bench of the Three Forks Formation. The curve was landed
at a measured depth of 10,651' at approximately 10,295' TVD with a projected inclination of
89.36°. An intermediate casing string consisting of 266 joints of 7" 32# HCP-110 was then set to
10,634' MD and cemented.
The lateral was drilled with one 6" Hughes T307 PDC bit ahead of a 1.5° Hunting motor to 15,618'
MD in 59.5 hours before being pulled for high torque. This assembly was replaced by a 6" Hughes
T406X PDC bit head of another 1.5° Hunting motor which drilled 2,883' in 37.5 hours before
being pulled after an MWD tool failure. The assembly was revised with an Ulterra U613M bit
ahead of another 1.5° Hunting motor and drilled 1,217' in 32 hours. A total depth of 19,718' MD
was reached at 04:08 CDT on September 9, 2014. The bottom hole location is 414.63' FNL and
1,258.78' FWL NW NW Section 20, T152N, R92W. Projected to TD, the wellbore is 9,701.57'
north and 118.78' east of the surface location with a closure direction of 0.70°, resulting in a
closure distance of 9,702.29'. Freshwater based drilling fluid was used while drilling the surface
hole, oil-based invert drilling fluid was utilized for the vertical and curve, while both saltwater and
oil-based drilling fluid was used for the lateral portion.
GEOLOGY
Methods
Geologic supervision was provided by a Sunburst Consulting, Inc. geology team, which logged
drill cuttings, monitored mud gas and provided on-site geo-steering consultation.
Geologic
evaluation began at 7,800' MD and continued until the well reached a total depth of 19,718' MD.
Rig crew members caught 30' lagged samples under direction of the well-site geologists. Cuttings
were examined under a binocular microscope, while cut fluorescence was observed under UV light
with Trichloroethylene, (Carbo-sol), cutting agent. Lithologic descriptions are provided as an
appendix to this report. A digital gas detector, (MLogger total gas with chromatograph), was
interfaced with a Pason electronic data recorder system. Pason provided depth, drill rates and pump
information to the gas detection computer and received total gas information for viewing around
location. Total gas was recorded as units (100 units = 1% methane equivalent in air) and
chromatography of C1­C4 components were calculated in parts-per-million.
Lithology and hydrocarbon shows
The siltstone and sandstone of the Big Snowy Group's Kibbey formation was present when
geologic evaluation began. The Kibbey `Lime' was not part of the geologic evaluation.
The Charles Salt was drilled at 7,950' MD, 7,949' TVD (-6,037'). This interval was identified by
translucent to transparent, trace milky, hard, euhedral to subhedral, crystalline salt with intervals
of white to off white, cream, trace light gray, microcrystalline, soft to friable, earthy limestone,
which was argillaceous in part, and white to off white, soft, massive, amorphous anhydrite (Figure
1).
Figure 1. Charles Salt [45x wet].
The Mission Canyon Formation was drilled at 8,661' MD, 8,660' TVD (-6,748') and consisted
of off white, cream, trace light gray, microcrystalline, soft to friable limestone that has an earthy
texture and is argillaceous in part (Figure 2).
Figure 2. Mission Canyon limestone [45x wet].
The Lodgepole Formation was drilled at 9,283' MD, 9,282' TVD (-7,370') and primarily
consisted of argillaceous limestone described as a mudstone that is light to medium brown, cream
to tan, trace light gray, crystalline and soft to friable with an earthy texture and trace disseminated
pyrite and trace amounts of an off white to cream, light gray, microcrystalline, earthy limestone
that is argillaceous in part and contained no visible porosity (Figure 3).
Figure 3. Lodgepole [45x wet].
The False Bakken was drilled at 10,128' MD, 10,089' TVD (-8,177') and was identified by a dark
gray, dark gray brown, soft to friable, blocky, carbonaceous shale with an earthy texture and
common disseminated pyrite (Figure 4).
Figure 4. False Bakken and Scallion [45x wet].
The Upper Bakken Shale was drilled at 10,146' MD, 10,102' TVD (-8,190') and consisted of a
dark gray, dark gray brown, soft to friable, blocky, earthy, petroliferous, carbonaceous shale which
contained common disseminated pyrite and no visible porosity (Figure 5).
Figure 5. Upper Bakken Shale [45x wet].
The Middle Bakken was penetrated at 10,175' MD, 10,121' TVD (-8,209'). This Bakken member
consisted of a light gray, light gray brown, trace medium gray, friable to firm, moderately sorted,
calcite and dolomitic cemented silty sandstone that contained trace disseminated pyrite and
exhibited trace intergranular porosity and trace spotty light brown oil stain (Figure 6).
Figure 6. Middle Bakken. [45x wet].
The Lower Bakken Shale was penetrated at 10,250' MD, 10,169' TVD (-8,257') and consisted
of a dark gray, dark gray brown, soft to friable, blocky, earthy, petroliferous, carbonaceous shale,
which contained common disseminated pyrite and no visible porosity (Figure 7).
Figure 7. Lower Bakken Shale. [45x wet].
The Three Forks Formation was penetrated at 10,328' MD, 10,212' TVD (-8,300'), while the
Three Forks Formation (second bench) was entered at 10,461' MD, 10,267' TVD (-8,355'). The
second bench target formation consisted of a sandy siltstone described as red brown, tan to light
brown, trace cream, blocky to sub blocky, poorly to moderately sorted, calcite cemented,
moderately cemented, with trace disseminated pyrite and trace light brown spotty oil stain and is
interbedded with a light to medium gray, light to medium gray brown, friable to firm, sub blocky
to blocky, earthy shale with trace disseminated pyrite (Figure 8).
Figure 8. Three Forks 2nd Bench. [45x wet].
Gas measurements (C1-C4) in the target zone were low throughout the lateral, with background
gases rising and/or falling dependent upon position within the target interval. Background gases
were consistently around 20 to 40 units though a majority of the lateral and increases to 100 to 120
units when the wellbore was in the upper part of the target interval, this pattern remained consistent
to TD (Figure 9). These gas levels were recorded against 9.7 to 10.3 lb/gal mud. Trace light brown
spotty oil staining was observed in samples throughout the lateral.
Figure 9. MController Three Forks (2nd Bench) interval indicating background gas with
corresponding chromatograph readings.
Geo-steering
The target zone was defined by the Slawson Exploration Company, Inc. project geologist as a 25'
thick interval beginning approximately 77' below the top of the Three Forks Formation, within the
second bench of the Three Forks, in an area of increased porosity. A TVD type log created by
Weatherford MWD (Figure 10) was utilized by Sunburst Consulting geologists to correlate the
gamma ray signature of formation markers during the steering of the lateral in order to determine
stratigraphic position and local apparent dip. In addition, samples, drilling parameters, type logs
and gas shows were interpreted to aid in the understanding of the wellbore's stratigraphic position.
Figure 10. Mooka 8-29-20TF2H target interval (Gerald Jett, Sunburst Consulting
geologist).
The drilling plan was to land 22' below the top of the second bench of the Three Forks Formation
within the area of higher porosity. From entry of the Three Forks second bench to TD a gross
apparent dip of 0.13° up was interpreted (Figure 11). On two occasions the wellbore exited the
base of zone, which at 10,761' MD the wellbore exited the base of the target and remained out of
zone until 11,013' MD and once again at 15,517' MD and remained out of zone until 16,303' MD.
After re-entering zone, the wellbore remained within the target interval until reaching total depth
at 19,718' MD.
Figure 11. Cross sectional interpretation of dip illustrating gas, MWD gamma ray and ROP.
SUMMARY
1)
Mooka 8-29-20TF2H was drilled to 19,718' MD with a lateral exposure of 9,067' in the
Three Forks second bench.
2)
The well spud on August 18, 2014 and was drilled from surface to total depth utilizing
seven bits in 274 drilling hours. The total depth was reached in 23 drilling days on
September 9, 2014.
3)
Diesel-based drilling fluid (8.50 to 11.00 lb/gal) was utilized from surface casing to a curve
landing of 10,651' MD. Both saltwater and oil based drilling fluid (9.7 to 10.3 lb/gal) were
successfully utilized throughout lateral portion of the well.
4)
The wellbore briefly exited the base of the Three Forks second bench target interval on two
separate occasions. The wellbore remained within the target zone for approximately 96%
of the lateral. An overall apparent dip of the target zone was estimated at 0.13° up.
5)
Background gas (C1-C4) was consistently around 20 to 40 units throughout a majority of
the lateral, dependent upon location in stratigraphy, and increased to 100 to 120 units in
the upper portion of the target interval. This pattern remained consistent to TD
6)
The Mooka 8-29-20TF2H is currently awaiting completion and enhanced stimulation
efforts to determine its ultimate production potential.
Respectfully submitted,
Gerald Jett
Lead Well Site Geologist and
Geo-steering Consultant
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
September 10, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Rig crews caught lagged samples, under the supervision of Sunburst geologists, in 30' intervals from 7,800' to
19,718' MD (TD). Gamma ray marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions below for reference.
Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope. Drilling fluid was diesel-based invert from
surface casing to an intermediate casing point of 10,651MD and both saltwater (displaced at 18,501' MD) and
diesel-based invert were utilized from intermediate casing to a total depth of 19,718' MD.
Drilling in Kibbey
7,800-7,830 ANHYDRITE: white-off white, soft, massive, amorphous; SILTSTONE reddish brown, trace light
brown, soft, blocky- subblocky, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible porosity
7,830-7,860 LIMESTONE: mudstone, off white, cream, trace light gray, microcrystalline, soft-friable, earthy
texture, argillaceous in part, no visible porosity; SILTSTONE reddish brown, trace light brown, soft, blocky-
subblocky, earthy texture, trace disseminated pyrite, no visible porosity
7,860-7,890 No sample
7,890-7,920 SILTSTONE: light red-red, soft, blocky, earthy texture; trace SANDSTONE: orange-light red, fine-
medium grained, friable- occasionally firm, subrounded, poorly-moderately sorted, dolomitic cement, moderately
cemented, silty in part
7,920-7,950 LIMESTONE: mudstone, white-off white, trace light gray, microcrystalline, soft, earthy texture, no
visible porosity; SALT: translucent-transparent, trace milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral-subhedral, crystalline texture
Charles Formation: 1st Salt
7,950' MD; 7,949' TVD (-6,037')
7,950-7,980 SALT: translucent-transparent, trace milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral-subhedral, crystalline texture
7,980-8,010 SALT: translucent-transparent, trace milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral-subhedral, crystalline texture
8,010-8,040 SALT: translucent-transparent, trace milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral-subhedral, crystalline texture
8,040-8,070 ANHYDRITE: white-off white, soft, massive, amorphous; LIMESTONE: mudstone, off white, cream,
trace light gray, microcrystalline, soft-friable, earthy texture, argillaceous in part, no visible porosity; trace SALT:
translucent-transparent, trace milky, crystalline, hard, euhedral-subhedral, crystalline texture
8,070-8,100 ANHYDRITE: white-off white, soft, massive, amorphous; trace SALT: translucent-transparent, trace

Dear Khem:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24606, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200'
setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre
spacing unit consisting of Sections 20 & 29 T152N, R92W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter
sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site
during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. SLAWSON
EXPLORATION COMPANY, INC. must take into consideration NDAC 43-02-03-28 (Safety Regulation)
when contemplating simultaneous operations on the above captioned location. Pursuant to NDAC 43-02-03-
28 (Safety Regulation) "No boiler, portable electric lighting generator, or treater shall be placed nearer than
150 feet to any producing well or oil tank." SLAWSON EXPLORATION must contact NDIC Field Inspector
Robert Garbe at 701-720-3262 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal
coordinate from the well head is: 9916 N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.

to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must
be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date
the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records
wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the
Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them,
complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to
any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any
information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so
obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission
and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

Slawson Pre-Frac Safety and Testing Procedure
7" casing testing procedure
1) Logging
a. Run bond log to top of L/H/P and ensure adequate cement coverage (at least 500' above top of zone to
be fractured)
b. Run casing inspection log in 7" casing to top of L/H/P or 100' beneath cement top
i. De-rate casing for any significant wear based on remaining wall thickness.
ii. Set maximum treating pressure at no more than 85% of the normal or de-rated pressure rating -
whichever applies.
2) Casing testing
a. RU wireline and set a test plug in the top of the Liner/Hanger/Packer.
b. Pressure test the 7" casing and wellhead as follows:
i. In new areas where treating pressures are unknown, test to 7500# for 30 minutes with less than
a 5% loss
ii. In areas with established operations, test to 500# above fracturing pressures seen in that area for
30 minutes with less than a 5% loss
iii. In the case of worn casing, if 85% of the de-rated pressure rating results in a maximum
allowable treating pressure that is less than 500# greater than the expected treating pressure ­
run a tie-back string
3) Pressure relief valve ­ an adequately sized pressure relief valve must be installed on the treating lines from
the pump to the wellhead and set to limit the line pressure to no more than the casing test pressure less 100#.
4) Surface casing valve ­ the surface casing valve must be left open and a diversion line run to a pit or
containment vessel; in order to enable relief of any pressure encountered in the surface casing/intermediate
casing annulus during fracture operations.
Fracturing Check List
1) Spot tanks
2) Install water manifold
3) Fill tanks
4) Add biocide and scale inhibitor and heat/mix water
5) Install 10,000# manually operated frac valve on tubing head
6) Install 10,000# remotely-activated, hydraulically-actuated valve
7) Install 10,000# frac tree
8) Install ball-catcher
9) RU flowback crew as much as possible
10) Stake lines down and secure all flowback equipment
11) Treat well
12) Initiate flowback and wait for sand to cleanup and oil cut to reach 15% before turning to the battery
13) After flowback is complete, shut well in and rig down the flowback crew
14) RD ball catcher and send back to Stinger
15) RD frac tree and send back to Frontier
16) RD hydraulically actuated valve and send back to Frontier
17) Leave manually operated master valve for well control
18) Turn well over to production
19) When it's time to run tubing, send manually operated master valve back to Frontier
The SHL is 440' FSL & 1,140' FWL (SWSW), Section 29, T152N, R92W, Mountrail
County, ND. The state setback from the section lines are 500' FEL & FWL, 200' FSL &
FNL.
